3. Architecture Recommendations
Process Architecture

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                  Main Process                     │
│  Express + tRPC + WebSocket + MCP Router          │
│  (orchestrates everything, never does heavy work) │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                   │
│  ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────┐  ┌──────────┐ │
│  │ Worker Pool │  │ MCP Server  │  │ File     │ │
│  │ (Agent      │  │ Child       │  │ Watchers │ │
│  │  Threads)   │  │ Processes   │  │          │ │
│  │             │  │             │  │ - Config │ │
│  │ - Each agent│  │ - stdio     │  │ - Session│ │
│  │   in own    │  │   transport │  │ - Memory │ │
│  │   thread    │  │ - crash     │  │          │ │
│  │ - Crash     │  │   isolated  │  │          │ │
│  │   isolated  │  │ - auto      │  │          │ │
│  │ - Shared    │  │   restart   │  │          │ │
│  │   memory    │  │             │  │          │ │
│  └─────────────┘  └─────────────┘  └──────────┘ │
│                                                   │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │            WebSocket Hub                      │ │
│  │  - Dashboard real-time updates                │ │
│  │  - Agent ↔ Agent communication                │ │
│  │  - Session streaming                          │ │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
Why TypeScript throughout (not Go/Java):

Dashboard compatibility — same language for backend and frontend, shared types via packages/types
MCP SDK — the official @modelcontextprotocol/sdk is TypeScript
Worker threads — Node.js worker threads provide process isolation without the complexity of polyglot
Child processes — MCP servers already run as child processes (stdio transport), providing natural isolation
tRPC — end-to-end type safety between backend and React dashboard
Ecosystem — virtually every AI tool SDK is TypeScript-first
For CPU-heavy tasks (embedding generation, large file processing), use:

Native Node.js addons (e.g., tree-sitter already uses WASM/native)
Child process delegation to Python scripts (for ML models)
Worker threads for parallel agent execution
Plugin Architecture

// packages/core/src/plugins/types.ts
interface HypercodePlugin {
  id: string;
  name: string;
  version: string;
  category: PluginCategory;
  
  // Lifecycle
  init(context: PluginContext): Promise<void>;
  destroy(): Promise<void>;
  
  // Optional: expose as MCP server
  mcpServer?: MCPServerDefinition;
  
  // Optional: expose dashboard panel
  dashboardPanel?: DashboardPanelDefinition;
  
  // Optional: expose CLI commands
  cliCommands?: CLICommandDefinition[];
  
  // Optional: expose tools for agentic loop
  tools?: ToolDefinition[];
}

type PluginCategory = 
  | 'memory'      // Memory backends (file, sqlite, chroma, etc.)
  | 'provider'    // AI providers (openai, anthropic, etc.)
  | 'tool'        // Tools (filesystem, browser, git, etc.)
  | 'transport'   // MCP transports (stdio, sse, http)
  | 'search'      // Search backends (ripgrep, semantic, ast)
  | 'rag'         // RAG pipelines (chunker, embedder, retriever)
  | 'extension';  // UI extensions
Each major subsystem (memory, providers, search, RAG) uses this plugin interface. Submodule code gets wrapped in a plugin adapter:


// Example: wrapping a memory submodule
// packages/memory/src/backends/claude-mem-adapter.ts
import { HypercodePlugin } from '@hypercode/core';

export const claudeMemPlugin: HypercodePlugin = {
  id: 'memory-claude-mem',
  name: 'Claude Memory Backend',
  version: '1.0.0',
  category: 'memory',
  
  async init(ctx) {
    // Initialize the claude-mem submodule's functionality
    // Either by importing its code directly or spawning it as a process
  },
  
  tools: [
    {
      name: 'memory_store',
      description: 'Store a memory using claude-mem backend',
      execute: async (params) => { /* ... */ }
    }
  ]
};
4. Submodule Strategy
Current State: 932+ Submodules
This is both a strength (massive reference library) and a liability (git performance, maintenance burden). Here's the strategy:

Tier System
Tier	Description	Count (est.)	Action
T1: Core Reference	Tools we're actively reaching feature parity with	~30	Keep updated, deeply document, wrap/integrate
T2: Plugin Candidates	Tools whose functionality we want as plugins	~50	Keep, create plugin adapters
T3: MCP Directory	MCP servers for our built-in directory	~200	Index metadata, don't need source
T4: Reference Only	Interesting but not actively used	~400	Document, consider removing submodule (keep link)
T5: Redundant/Stale	Duplicates or abandoned	~250	Remove submodule, keep in link index
T1 Core References (Feature Parity Targets)

CLI/TUI Coding Tools:
├── opencode           # Plugin system, multi-provider, LSP, web terminal
├── claude-code        # Agentic loop reference, tool use patterns  
├── codex-cli          # Sandboxed execution
├── gemini-cli         # Large context, multi-modal
├── goose-cli          # Extensible toolkits
├── copilot-cli        # GitHub integration
├── crush              # TUI beauty reference
├── codebuff           # Speed/efficiency reference
├── kilocode           # Cost tracking reference
├── trae-cli           # Project understanding

MCP Ecosystem:
├── metamcp            # Master MCP aggregator (upstream only)
├── mcp-superassistant # Browser extension bridge
├── mcpm               # MCP package manager
├── mcp-get            # MCP installation
├── toolhive           # MCP container management

Memory/RAG:
├── claude-mem         # Structural memory
├── mem0               # Structured memory service
├── supermemory        # Cloud memory
├── letta              # Agent memory
├── zep                # Conversation memory

Agent Frameworks:
├── jules-autopilot    # Cloud dev agent (upstream only)
├── deerflow           # LangGraph super agent
├── mastra             # Agent framework
├── openai-agents-sdk  # OpenAI agents reference
├── google-adk         # Google agent dev kit
5. Dashboard Implementation Plan
The dashboard is the primary interface for Hypercode. Every feature must be accessible through it. Here's the panel structure:

Navigation Structure

Sidebar:
├── 🏠 Overview (system health, quick stats, recent activity)
├── 💻 Sessions (active coding sessions, history, import/export)
├── 🤖 Agents (agent library, spawn, manage, live chat)
├── 🔌 MCP (server management, traffic inspector, directory, config)
├── 🧠 Memory (browse, search, import/export, visualization)
├── 📊 Providers (quotas, OAuth, fallback chains, billing)
├── 🛠️ Tools (tool browser, status, install, groups)
├── 📦 Skills (skill library, install, convert)
├── 🔍 Search (semantic code search, RAG query)
├── 🐝 Swarm (missions, governance, risk analytics)
├── 📖 Prompts (prompt library, templates, system prompts)
├── 🌐 Browser (extension status, memory capture, web search)
├── ⚙️ Settings (config, env vars, secrets, about)
└── 📋 Logs (activity log, audit trail, error log)
Overview Panel (Landing Page)
This is the most important panel — it must give instant situational awareness:


// apps/web/src/pages/overview.tsx
export function OverviewPanel() {
  return (
    <div className="grid grid-cols-12 gap-4">
      {/* Row 1: System vitals */}
      <SystemHealthStrip />        {/* CPU, RAM, GPU, Disk, Network */}
      
      {/* Row 2: Active work */}
      <ActiveSessionsCard />       {/* Currently running sessions with model/status */}
      <ProviderQuotaCard />        {/* Visual quota bars per provider */}
      
      {/* Row 3: Infrastructure */}
      <MCPServerStatusCard />      {/* Active MCP servers with latency */}
      <MemoryStatsCard />          {/* Memory count, last harvest, backends */}
      <ToolStatusCard />           {/* Installed tools with version status */}
      
      {/* Row 4: Activity */}
      <RecentActivityFeed />       {/* Last 20 events across all subsystems */}
      
      {/* Row 5: Quick actions */}
      <QuickActionBar />           {/* New Session, Quick Task, Install Tool */}
    </div>
  );
}

6. Implementation Sequence
Here's the concrete implementation order for the next sprint:

Sprint 1: Provider Fallback + Agentic Loop (Phase 122-123)
Files to create/modify:

7. Key Design Decisions & Rationale
Decision	Choice	Rationale
Language	TypeScript throughout	Shared types, MCP SDK native, dashboard compatibility, developer ecosystem
Process isolation	Worker threads for agents, child processes for MCP servers	Crash isolation without polyglot complexity
State management	tRPC + React Query + WebSocket	End-to-end type safety, real-time updates, optimistic UI
Memory default	SQLite + ChromaDB hybrid	SQLite for structured data (fast, zero-config), ChromaDB for vectors (semantic search)
MCP strategy	Be both client AND server	Aggregate external servers, expose unified interface to any MCP client
Submodule strategy	Tiered (T1-T5)	Active integration for core refs, index-only for directory entries, remove redundant
Plugin architecture	Interface-based with lifecycle hooks	Each subsystem (memory, provider, search) pluggable without monolithic coupling
Dashboard framework	Next.js (existing)	Already in use, SSR for initial load, API routes for OAuth callbacks
Config format	JSONC everywhere	Comments essential for self-documenting configs
Version source	Single VERSION file	Avoids drift between VERSION.md, package.json, hypercode.config.json
8. Immediate Next Actions
Given the current state, here are the concrete next steps in priority order:

Phases 100-121 added increasingly marginal governance analytics. Freeze swarm features and redirect all effort to core value proposition.

1. Multi-Core Fault-Tolerant Architecture
Decision: Pure TypeScript/Node.js with Strategic Process Isolation

Given the dashboard/browser compatibility requirement and the MCP ecosystem's Node.js dominance, we stay TypeScript-native. However, we implement a "Cellular Architecture" for crash isolation and core utilization:

Process Topology

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    HYPERCODE MASTER PROCESS                      │
│  (Express + tRPC + WebSocket + MCP Router Core)             │
│  - HTTP API/WebSocket hub                                   │
│  - Configuration management                                 │
│  - Database connections (SQLite/Postgres)                   │
└──────────────┬──────────────────────────────┬───────────────┘
               │                              │
    ┌──────────▼──────────┐      ┌───────────▼────────────┐
    │   AGENT WORKERS     │      │   MCP SERVER POOL      │
    │   (Worker Threads)  │      │   (Child Processes)    │
    │  • Isolated v8 ctx  │      │  • stdio/SSE bridges   │
    │  • Per-agent memory │      │  • Auto-restart logic  │
    │  • Crash isolation  │      │  • Health monitoring   │
    │  • Model clients    │      │  • Namespace grouping  │
    └──────────┬──────────┘      └───────────┬────────────┘
               │                              │
    ┌──────────▼──────────────────────────────▼────────────┐
    │              REDIS MESH BUS (Pub/Sub)                │
    │   • Swarm coordination                               │
    │   • Cross-process state sync                         │
    │   • Artifact federation                              │
    └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
Key Architectural Patterns
1. Agent Worker Threads (isolated v8 contexts)

Each AI model instance runs in a Worker thread
SharedArrayBuffer for zero-copy context passing
Uncaught exceptions kill only the worker, not the master
Auto-restart with exponential backoff via HealerService
2. MCP Server Child Process Pool

Each MCP server is a forked process (stdio transport)
McpProcessManager handles lifecycle: start, health-check, restart, SIGTERM
Proxy pattern converts stdio↔SSE↔StreamableHTTP as needed
Namespace isolation via virtual prefixes (code.github, memory.sqlite)
3. Crash Boundaries

Level 1: Try/catch around tool calls (expected errors)
Level 2: Worker termination + respawn (model crashes)
Level 3: Process restart + session recovery (MCP server crashes)
Level 4: Circuit breakers to prevent cascade failures
4. Language Strategy

Core: TypeScript (API, routing, state management)
Heavy compute: Rust sidecars only if needed for tree-sitter parsing at scale (optional future optimization)
CLI tools: Wrap existing binaries (opencode, aider, etc.) via Node.js child_process with PTY support
2. Core Engine Consolidation Strategy
Instead of maintaining forks of metamcp and jules-autopilot, we assimilate their functionality into packages/core:

Phase A: MCP Master Router (Week 1-2)
Implement the MetaMCP functionality natively:

Dynamic Tool Registry: In-memory Map + SQLite persistence
Transport Adapters: stdio, SSE, StreamableHTTP with automatic conversion
Progressive Disclosure: Load tools on-demand based on semantic similarity to current task
TOON Formatter: Convert JSON schemas to minimized context representations
Traffic Inspector: Circular buffer of last 1000 MCP messages with tRPC streaming to dashboard
Phase B: Autopilot Engine (Week 3-4)
Port jules-autopilot capabilities:

Session Durable Objects: SQLite-backed state machines for each dev session
Plan/Execute/Verify Loop: Structured output parsing with rollback capability
Git Worktree Manager: Automatic worktree creation per task (Phase 95 already done, extend for cloud dev)
Cloud Dev Bridge: Jules/Codex/Devin API integration with local file sync
Phase C: Model Fallback Router (Critical - Week 1)
Priority P0: Implement the quota-aware model router immediately to prevent blocking:


// packages/core/src/ai/ModelFallbackRouter.ts
interface FallbackChain {
  primary: ModelConfig;      // e.g., Claude 4 Opus
  fallbacks: ModelConfig[];  // [Gemini 2.5 Pro, GPT-5, DeepSeek-V3...]
  quotaTracker: QuotaService; // Tracks usage across providers
}

class ModelFallbackRouter {
  async executeWithFallback(task: Task, chain: FallbackChain): Promise<Result> {
    for (const model of [chain.primary, ...chain.fallbacks]) {
      try {
        return await this.execute(task, model);
      } catch (e) {
        if (e.code === 'QUOTA_EXCEEDED' || e.code === 'RATE_LIMIT') {
          await this.quotaTracker.markExhausted(model.provider);
          continue;
        }
        throw e;
      }
    }
    throw new Error('All models exhausted');
  }
}

1. 🏗️ Architecture Decision: TypeScript vs. Go/Java
Decision: Stay with TypeScript/Node.js.

Reasoning:

Ecosystem Compatibility: The AI tooling landscape (MCP SDKs, Vercel AI SDK, LangChain, CLI tools like Opencode/Claude Code) is predominantly JavaScript/TypeScript. Wrapping or importing these is seamless in Node.
Dashboard Unity: Using React/Next.js for the WebUI and Node.js for the Core allows shared types (packages/types), shared logic, and single-language maintenance.
Concurrency Model: Node.js worker_threads and child_process provide sufficient isolation for agent tasks. We do not need Go/Java unless we hit specific CPU-bound bottlenecks (e.g., heavy embedding generation), which can be offloaded to specialized services or native addons.
Speed of Development: The "Assimilate" philosophy requires rapid integration of new features. TS allows faster iteration than compiled statically-typed languages for this specific domain.
Stability Strategy:

Worker Threads: Run each AI Model Session in an isolated worker_thread.
Process Supervision: Use a SessionGuardian service to monitor workers and restart on crash.
Memory Isolation: Each worker gets its own context heap; shared state via MessagePort only.
2. 📋 Phase 122 Implementation Plan
3. 💻 Code Scaffolding & Implementation
3.1 Core Service: QuotaAwareProviderService
This service handles the automatic fallback logic.


// packages/core/src/services/QuotaAwareProviderService.ts
import { EventEmitter } from 'events';
import { ModelProvider, ModelConfig } from '../types/providers';
import { Logger } from '../utils/Logger';

interface QuotaStatus {
  provider: string;
  remaining: number;
  resetAt: Date;
  isExhausted: boolean;
}

export class QuotaAwareProviderService extends EventEmitter {
  private providers: ModelProvider[];
  private currentProviderIndex: number = 0;
  private quotaStatus: Map<string, QuotaStatus> = new Map();
  private logger: Logger;

  constructor(providers: ModelProvider[]) {
    super();
    this.providers = providers;
    this.logger = new Logger('QuotaAwareProviderService');
    this.initializeQuotaTracking();
  }

  private initializeQuotaTracking() {
    // Initialize status for all providers
    this.providers.forEach(p => {
      this.quotaStatus.set(p.id, {
        provider: p.id,
        remaining: p.quotaLimit || Infinity,
        resetAt: p.quotaReset || new Date(Date.now() + 86400000),
        isExhausted: false
      });
    });
  }

  public async getAvailableProvider(): Promise<ModelProvider> {
    let attempts = 0;
    while (attempts < this.providers.length) {
      const provider = this.providers[this.currentProviderIndex];
      const status = this.quotaStatus.get(provider.id);

      if (status && !status.isExhausted) {
        this.logger.info(`Selected provider: ${provider.id}`);
        return provider;
      }

      // Rotate to next provider
      this.currentProviderIndex = (this.currentProviderIndex + 1) % this.providers.length;
      attempts++;
    }

    throw new Error('All providers exhausted. Please check quotas.');
  }

  public reportQuotaExhausted(providerId: string) {
    const status = this.quotaStatus.get(providerId);
    if (status) {
      status.isExhausted = true;
      this.quotaStatus.set(providerId, status);
      this.emit('provider_exhausted', { providerId, timestamp: new Date() });
      this.logger.warn(`Provider ${providerId} exhausted. Rotating fallback.`);
    }
  }

  public resetQuota(providerId: string) {
    const status = this.quotaStatus.get(providerId);
    if (status) {
      status.isExhausted = false;
      status.remaining = this.providers.find(p => p.id === providerId)?.quotaLimit || Infinity;
      this.quotaStatus.set(providerId, status);
      this.emit('provider_reset', { providerId });
    }
  }
}
3.2 Core Service: SessionGuardian
This service supervises CLI sessions (Opencode, Claude, etc.) and ensures auto-restart.


// packages/core/src/services/SessionGuardian.ts
import { spawn, ChildProcess } from 'child_process';
import { EventEmitter } from 'events';
import { SessionConfig } from '../types/sessions';

export class SessionGuardian extends EventEmitter {
  private activeSessions: Map<string, ChildProcess> = new Map();
  private sessionConfigs: Map<string, SessionConfig> = new Map();
  private heartbeatInterval: number = 5000; // 5 seconds

  public startSession(sessionId: string, config: SessionConfig) {
    this.sessionConfigs.set(sessionId, config);
    this.spawnProcess(sessionId, config);
  }

  private spawnProcess(sessionId: string, config: SessionConfig) {
    const [cmd, ...args] = config.command.split(' ');
    
    const child = spawn(cmd, args, {
      env: { ...process.env, ...config.env },
      cwd: config.cwd,
      stdio: ['pipe', 'pipe', 'pipe']
    });

    this.activeSessions.set(sessionId, child);
    this.emit('session_started', { sessionId, pid: child.pid });

    // Monitor stdout/stderr for WebUI streaming
    child.stdout?.on('data', (data) => this.emit('session_log', { sessionId, data, type: 'stdout' }));
    child.stderr?.on('data', (data) => this.emit('session_log', { sessionId, data, type: 'stderr' }));

    // Handle Crash/Exit
    child.on('exit', (code) => {
      this.emit('session_exit', { sessionId, code });
      if (config.autoRestart) {
        this.logger.warn(`Session ${sessionId} crashed (code ${code}). Restarting...`);
        setTimeout(() => this.spawnProcess(sessionId, config), 2000);
      }
    });
  }

  public stopSession(sessionId: string) {
    const child = this.activeSessions.get(sessionId);
    if (child) {
      child.kill();
      this.activeSessions.delete(sessionId);
      this.emit('session_stopped', { sessionId });
    }
  }

  public restartSession(sessionId: string) {
    this.stopSession(sessionId);
    const config = this.sessionConfigs.get(sessionId);
    if (config) {
      this.startSession(sessionId, config);
    }
  }
}
3.3 WebUI Component: MissionControlDashboard
A React component aggregating system health and session status.


// apps/web/src/components/dashboard/MissionControlDashboard.tsx
import React, { useEffect, useState } from 'react';
import { Card, CardHeader, CardTitle, CardContent } from '@/components/ui/card';
import { Badge } from '@/components/ui/badge';
import { Activity, Server, Terminal, AlertCircle } from 'lucide-react';

interface SystemStats {
  cpu: number;
  ram: number;
  disk: number;
  activeSessions: number;
}

export function MissionControlDashboard() {
  const [stats, setStats] = useState<SystemStats>({ cpu: 0, ram: 0, disk: 0, activeSessions: 0 });
  const [sessions, setSessions] = useState<any[]>([]);

  useEffect(() => {
    // WebSocket connection to core for real-time updates
    const ws = new WebSocket('ws://localhost:3001/ws/mission-control');
    ws.onmessage = (event) => {
      const data = JSON.parse(event.data);
      if (data.type === 'stats') setStats(data.payload);
      if (data.type === 'sessions') setSessions(data.payload);
    };
    return () => ws.close();
  }, []);

  return (
    <div className="grid grid-cols-1 md:grid-cols-2 lg:grid-cols-4 gap-4 p-4">
      {/* System Health */}
      <Card className="bg-slate-900 border-slate-700 text-white">
        <CardHeader className="flex flex-row items-center justify-between space-y-0 pb-2">
          <CardTitle className="text-sm font-medium">CPU Usage</CardTitle>
          <Activity className="h-4 w-4 text-green-400" />
        </CardHeader>
        <CardContent>
          <div className="text-2xl font-bold">{stats.cpu}%</div>
          <p className="text-xs text-slate-400">Real-time monitoring</p>
        </CardContent>
      </Card>

      {/* Active Sessions */}
      <Card className="bg-slate-900 border-slate-700 text-white">
        <CardHeader className="flex flex-row items-center justify-between space-y-0 pb-2">
          <CardTitle className="text-sm font-medium">Active Sessions</CardTitle>
          <Terminal className="h-4 w-4 text-blue-400" />
        </CardHeader>
        <CardContent>
          <div className="text-2xl font-bold">{stats.activeSessions}</div>
          <p className="text-xs text-slate-400">Supervised by Guardian</p>
        </CardContent>
      </Card>

      {/* Session List */}
      <Card className="col-span-1 md:col-span-2 lg:col-span-2 bg-slate-900 border-slate-700 text-white">
        <CardHeader>
          <CardTitle>Session Orchestrator</CardTitle>
        </CardHeader>
        <CardContent>
          <div className="space-y-2">
            {sessions.map(session => (
              <div key={session.id} className="flex items-center justify-between p-2 bg-slate-800 rounded">
                <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
                  <Badge variant={session.status === 'running' ? 'default' : 'destructive'}>
                    {session.status}
                  </Badge>
                  <span className="font-mono text-sm">{session.name}</span>
                </div>
                <div className="flex gap-2">
                  <button className="text-xs bg-slate-700 px-2 py-1 rounded hover:bg-slate-600">Logs</button>
                  <button className="text-xs bg-slate-700 px-2 py-1 rounded hover:bg-slate-600">Restart</button>
                </div>
              </div>
            ))}
          </div>
        </CardContent>
      </Card>
    </div>
  );
}

Given the repo state and the scope, the right answer is not “rewrite everything in Go/Java.”
The right answer is:

Recommendation: Keep Hypercode primarily in TypeScript, with isolated worker/process boundaries
Use:

TypeScript/Node.js for:
core orchestration
WebUI backend/API
plugin runtime
MCP router/client/server
session manager
provider management
most tool wrappers
dashboard event bus
Worker threads + child processes for isolation
Python sidecars only where Python is already best-in-class
RAG/document pipelines
browser/computer use tools
specialized ML pipelines
Optional Rust/Go microservices later only for proven bottlenecks
transport proxy
high-volume traffic inspection
embeddings queue / indexing engine
heavy log/event stream processing
For your current product goals, TypeScript-first is the best architectural choice because it preserves:

shared types across backend and frontend
fastest feature iteration
direct reuse of existing code in repo/submodules
easiest WebUI integration
easiest plugin and MCP integration
simplest maintainability for a very wide surface area
Short answer to your language question
Should you use Go or Java?
Not as the main architecture.

Use TypeScript for the platform core.
Because you need:

browser/dashboard compatibility
rapid integration of many toolchains
shared schemas/types
plugin flexibility
MCP/client/server support
easiest reuse of current codebase
Use Go only if later you identify a narrow systems bottleneck:
high-performance proxy daemon
long-running multiplexed MCP transport
telemetry collector
process supervisor agent for OS-level control
Use Java basically never here unless:
you are integrating an existing Java ecosystem dependency
you need enterprise JVM infra for a separate service
For Hypercode, Java would add complexity without meaningful product advantage.

The architecture you actually want
Core principle
Hypercode should be a plugin-capable operating system kernel for AI tooling, where every capability can exist in one or more of these forms:

Native internal implementation
Wrapped external library/submodule implementation
MCP-exposed implementation
CLI/session-controlled implementation
Dashboard-managed service
That means MCP is one transport/interface, not the architecture itself.

Proposed architecture
1. Layered system design
Layer A — Control Plane
This is the long-running Hypercode brain.

Responsibilities:

session registry
process supervision
provider registry
model routing and fallback
tool registry
plugin registry
MCP registry
policy engine
auth/secret management
event bus
telemetry aggregation
dashboard API
Suggested home:

packages/core
possibly split into:
packages/orchestrator
packages/runtime
packages/providers
packages/mcp
packages/sessions
Layer B — Execution Plane
This is where actual work happens, isolated from the control plane.

Execution units:

model tasks
agent tasks
CLI harness sessions
code execution sandbox
MCP server child processes
browser/computer-use tasks
research crawlers/indexers
Isolation modes:

worker thread for CPU-light, memory-shared structured execution
child process for untrusted or crash-prone adapters
containerized sidecar for heavy or external-service tasks
Rule of thumb:

Worker threads
agent planning
structured orchestration tasks
parsing/ranking pipelines
Child processes
CLI tools
MCP servers
browser automators
code execution
anything that may crash/hang
Python sidecars
OCR
some RAG ingestion
langgraph-style systems
browser-use style integrations
Layer C — Integration Plane
Everything external gets normalized here.

Includes:

provider adapters
CLI harness adapters
MCP adapters
memory backend adapters
RAG adapters
auth adapters
browser adapters
git/worktree adapters
This layer converts external systems into a Hypercode-native contract.

Example normalized contracts:

ModelProvider
ToolProvider
MemoryBackend
SessionRuntime
ResearchSource
AuthProvider
BrowserBridge
Layer D — Experience Plane
This is the UI/UX layer.

Primary surfaces:

WebUI dashboard
CLI
browser extension
optional minimal TUI
Your own prompt says the WebUI should be first-class and probably primary. I agree.

So the architecture should treat the WebUI not as a bolt-on, but as the main operator console.

The concurrency model you want
Goal
You asked:

how should our architecture be so each model runs on a different thread, uses many cores efficiently, and one crash doesn’t kill the whole system?

Correct answer
Do not put each model in a raw JS thread and hope for the best.

Instead:

Use a 3-tier execution isolation model
Tier 1 — Orchestration thread
Main process:

dashboard API
event bus
scheduling
registry state
supervision
health aggregation
This process should stay lean and avoid heavy execution.

Tier 2 — Worker thread pool
For:

prompt construction
ranking
planning
summarization
policy checks
context compaction
lightweight agent logic
Benefits:

parallel CPU usage
lower overhead than spawning processes
good for trusted internal code
Tier 3 — Child process/session runtime
For:

each autonomous session
each external CLI harness
each MCP server instance
browser automation
sandboxed code execution
Benefits:

crash isolation
kill/restart ability
stdout/stderr capture
timeout enforcement
memory accounting
This gives you the actual “AI OS” reliability behavior.

Recommended runtime topology
Main services
1. CoreControlService
The central coordinator.

Responsibilities:

maintain system state
expose API/WebSocket
launch runtimes
supervise health
persist session metadata
route model requests
2. ExecutionSupervisor
Responsible for starting/stopping/restarting workloads.

Manages:

agent workers
CLI sessions
MCP server child processes
browser runtimes
scheduled research/index jobs
Features:

restart policy
exponential backoff
crash loop detection
resource ceilings
health probes
3. ProviderRouter
This is one of your most important missing “must-have now” features.

Responsibilities:

model selection
quota tracking
fallback chains
provider scoring
task-based routing
cost/speed/quality heuristics
This should become a first-class subsystem, not incidental code.

Core algorithm inputs:

task type
required capabilities
max budget
latency preference
current quotas
recent failures
model performance history
auth availability
subscription availability
Outputs:

selected provider/model
fallback chain
rationale telemetry
4. SessionRuntimeManager
Manages long-running harness sessions.

Session types:

Hypercode-native coding agent
wrapped CLI harness session
cloud remote session
browser-attached session
swarm mission session
It should support:

resume
snapshot
restart
worktree binding
repo binding
provider binding
supervisor policies
council oversight
crash continuation
5. ToolRuntimeManager
Responsible for:

internal tools
wrapped tools
MCP-exposed tools
tool policies
permission boundaries
telemetry
semantic registry
6. KnowledgeIngestionManager
For all your “research every link, categorize, summarize, index, submodule/reference” requirements.

This should be an explicit pipeline:

URL discovery
dedupe
fetch
classify
summarize
extract repo/docs/issues/features
score relevance
decide: submodule / mirror / index-only / reject
store in universal library index
emit docs pages and structured records
This is not a side task. It is an actual product subsystem.

Folder/package structure I recommend
A more reality-aligned structure than the current giant blended surface:


apps/
  web/                      # Primary dashboard
  extension/                # Browser extension
  cli/                      # Thin CLI operator client

packages/
  core/                     # API, orchestration entrypoint, event bus
  runtime/                  # ExecutionSupervisor, worker/process management
  providers/                # ProviderRouter, quota/fallback/auth
  sessions/                 # SessionRuntimeManager, session persistence
  agents/                   # Director, Council, Supervisor, Swarm logic
  tools/                    # Internal tools + wrappers + policy engine
  mcp/                      # MCP client/server/router/proxy/registry
  memory/                   # Memory abstraction + backend adapters
  rag/                      # Ingestion, chunking, embeddings, retrieval
  research/                 # Link crawler, repo analyzer, docs/index pipeline
  auth/                     # OAuth, tokens, secrets, env management
  telemetry/                # Metrics, events, logs, health, traces
  git/                      # Worktrees, repo indexing, git ops
  browser/                  # Browser-use bridge, extension backend APIs
  plugins/                  # Plugin SDK + runtime loader
  schemas/                  # Shared zod schemas and types
  ui-contracts/             # Shared DTOs for dashboard
  harnesses/                # Adapters for opencode/codex/claude/gemini/etc

services/
  python-rag/               # Optional Python sidecar
  browser-automation/       # Optional Python/Playwright sidecar
  system-proxy/             # Optional future high-performance service
Plugin system design
You explicitly want functionality to be built in, but also pluggable and optionally MCP-exposed.

That means every major capability should implement a common internal contract.

Example plugin categories
Provider plugins
Tool plugins
Memory backend plugins
RAG ingestion plugins
Session runtime plugins
CLI harness plugins
Auth plugins
Browser integration plugins
Research/index plugins
Core rule
Each plugin should support some or all of these modes:

Mode	Meaning
Native	Internal TS implementation
Wrapped	Calls external code/lib/submodule
Process	Launches external executable
MCP	Exposes or consumes via MCP
UI-managed	Has dashboard controls and telemetry
That lets you implement redundancy without chaos.

How to represent external tools like Opencode, Claude Code, Codex, etc.
You said you no longer necessarily want Hypercode to control them from the outside as the primary model. I think that is right.

So treat those tools as:

HarnessAdapters
Each adapter describes:

how to start session
how to send prompt/task
how to capture output
how to detect crash/hang
how to resume/restart
how to bind repo/worktree
how to observe token/model/provider usage
how to inject supervisor/council oversight
whether it supports browser/web control
whether it should be wrapped, referenced, or only parity-targeted
Example interface:


interface HarnessAdapter {
  id: string;
  displayName: string;
  capabilities: HarnessCapabilities;

  detect(): Promise<DetectionResult>;
  startSession(input: StartSessionInput): Promise<SessionHandle>;
  sendMessage(sessionId: string, input: HarnessMessage): Promise<HarnessResponse>;
  pauseSession(sessionId: string): Promise<void>;
  resumeSession(sessionId: string): Promise<void>;
  stopSession(sessionId: string): Promise<void>;
  getSessionState(sessionId: string): Promise<SessionState>;
  getTelemetry(sessionId: string): Promise<HarnessTelemetry>;
}
Hypercode-native harness should be the preferred implementation.
External adapters are compatibility bridges and feature references.

Automatic model fallback: make this a first-class engine now
You specifically said this is one of the most important immediate features. I agree.

Build a FallbackPolicyEngine
This should support:

ordered fallback chains
task-specific fallback chains
provider-level failover
quota exhaustion detection
auth failure rerouting
rate-limit cooldown windows
“stay on same family if possible”
“prefer free/subscription-backed models before API-billed”
“prefer fast planner then strong implementer”
“switch only for implementation, keep planner fixed”
manual pinning override
budget ceiling
quality floor
Example policy

{
  "policyId": "default-coding",
  "strategy": "capability_first_with_quota_fallback",
  "preferred": [
    "anthropic:claude-opus",
    "openai:gpt-5-codex",
    "google:gemini-2.5-pro",
    "openrouter:claude-opus",
    "copilot:gpt-4.1",
    "local:qwen-coder"
  ],
  "onRateLimit": "fallback-next",
  "onQuotaExhausted": "fallback-next",
  "onAuthFailure": "skip-provider",
  "onToolUseMismatch": "fallback-capability-match",
  "budget": {
    "maxCostUsd": 10
  }
}

fallback chain editor

model availability heatmap
failure reasons stream
“why this model was chosen” panel
per-session provider lock / auto mode toggle
simulation mode: “if current model fails, what happens next?”
This would be one of the highest-value UI features in the whole app.

Best execution model for stability
Use event sourcing lite
Do not rely on in-memory state only.

Store key domain events:

session started
session crashed
restart attempted
model selected
fallback triggered
tool denied
memory harvested
repo indexed
source researched
submodule added
docs mirrored
provider auth changed
This gives you:

dashboard replay/history
debugging
auditability
resumability
better recovery after restart
You do not need full formal event sourcing everywhere.
But for the AI-OS style system, a durable event log is extremely valuable.

Strong recommendation on process isolation
For your “many sessions, many tools, don’t crash the system” requirement:

Every long-running autonomous unit should have:
unique runtime ID
health state
heartbeat timestamp
restart policy
max restart count
crash loop detection
attached logs

provider binding
memory usage sample
CPU sample
active operation info
This is basically Hypercode’s equivalent of a process table.

Suggested technical primitives
Backend
Node.js + TypeScript
worker_threads
child_process

Queues
Use a queue abstraction for:

research jobs

indexing
model tasks
background sync jobs
Could be:

in-process first
Redis-backed when needed
What not to do
Do not:
try to fully reimplement every referenced tool at once
bind UI directly to arbitrary backend routers forever
rely on one giant Node process for all workloads
make MCP the only execution path
create feature parity via undocumented wrappers
add submodules without structured indexing/research metadata
mix “reference” and “runtime dependency” status without explicit labels
Prioritized implementation order
You asked to continue pragmatically. Here is the right order.

Phase A — Stability and operator control
Highest value immediately.

ProviderRouter + FallbackPolicyEngine
SessionRuntimeManager
ExecutionSupervisor

Phase E — Harness parity
Hypercode-native coding harness maturity
Adapters for external harnesses
supervisor/council oversight for sessions
web-managed external CLI session orchestration
Answer to “should each model run on a different thread?”
Better framing:
Each task/runtime should run in the right isolation boundary.

Good mapping
planner/debate logic → worker thread
actual provider call → async task within worker or child session runtime
long-running autonomous coding session → child process
browser/computer use → child process or sidecar
untrusted external CLI → child process
heavy indexing pipeline → worker thread pool or sidecar
So: not literally one model = one thread, but one runtime unit = isolated execution container appropriate to risk and workload.

That is the scalable answer.

If you want one sentence architecture summary
Build Hypercode as a TypeScript-first AI operating system kernel with a durable control plane, isolated execution runtimes, a plugin-based capability model, and a WebUI-first operator dashboard; use MCP as one interface among many, not the sole implementation path.

Concrete next-step recommendation
If I were driving implementation next, I would do this immediately:

Next 5 concrete deliverables
Create ProviderRouter and FallbackPolicyEngine as explicit packages/services
Create ExecutionSupervisor with child-process lifecycle management
Create a unified SessionRuntime schema and runtime registry
Refactor WebUI top nav into operator domains: Mission Control / Sessions / Providers / Tools / Memory / Research
Add a Library Index subsystem for link/repo research tracking and integration decisions
These five changes would align the architecture with your actual long-term vision better than another scattered batch of feature additions.

If you want, I can next turn this into a concrete target monorepo architecture document for Hypercode, including:

package-by-package responsibilities

data flow

phased implementation plan tied to your existing repo structure
or I can produce a feature-parity execution roadmap specifically for:

provider fallback/session supervision first.

// Example: New Missions Governance Strip (apps/web/src/components/Missions/GovernanceStrip.tsx)
import { api } from '@/utils/trpc';
import { Card, Badge, Slider } from '@/components/ui';

export const GovernanceStrip = ({ filters }: { filters: MissionFilters }) => {
  const { data: facets } = api.missions.riskFacets.useQuery(filters);
  if (!facets) return <div>Loading...</div>;

  return (
    <Card className="grid grid-cols-[1fr_auto_1fr] gap-4 p-4 bg-gradient-to-r from-purple-900/50 to-blue-900/50">
      <div>
        <h3>Dominant Risk: {facets.dominantBand} ({facets.percentages.dominant}%)</h3>
        <Badge variant={facets.health.severity === 'HIGH' ? 'destructive' : 'default'}>
          Health: {facets.health.score}/100 ({facets.health.confidence.level})
        </Badge>
      </div>
      <Slider
        value={[facets.filters.minRisk || 0, 100]}
        onValueChange={(v) => updateFilters({ minRisk: v[0] })}
        max={100}
        step={1}
        className="self-center"
      />
      <div className="text-right">
        <p>Denied Events (24h): {facets.momentum.trend > 0 ? '↑' : '↓'} {facets.denied24h}</p>
        <p>Recommended: {facets.health.action}</p>
      </div>
    </Card>
  );
};
New Panels:
MCP Traffic Inspector: Live JSON-RPC log (latency/dir/method).
Provider Fallback Chain Editor: Drag-drop models; quota viz.
Memory Converter: Import claude-mem → pgvector.
Swarm Risk Triage: Filter/sort (risk-first); facets health panel.
Accessibility: Tooltips/JSDoc everywhere; Keyboard nav; Mobile-responsive.
Docs Inline: Every tab → Collapsible <details> w/ features list.

### Phase 122 (P0): Fallback + Supervision (must ship first)
- `ProviderRouter` + `FallbackPolicyEngine`

### 1. The Mathematical Fallback & Quota Engine 

To make Hypercode completely autonomous, it must never halt due to a `429 Rate Limit` or `402 Quota Exceeded`. We are implementing an intelligent scoring algorithm in the `FallbackOrchestrator`.

The cost and quota tracking will be handled mathematically in the background:
The total session cost is aggregated across all $n$ tool calls and agent loops:
$$Cost_{session} = \sum_{i=1}^{n} \left( T_{in}^{(i)} \cdot C_{in} + T_{out}^{(i)} \cdot C_{out} \right)$$
*(Where $T$ is tokens and $C$ is cost per token for the specific provider).*

When selecting the next model in the fallback chain, the router calculates a selection weight $W$ based on available quota $Q$ and current usage $U$:
$W_{model} = \max(0, Q_{model} - U_{model}) \times \text{CapabilityScore}$
If $W_{model} \le 0$, the router instantly cascades to the next provider (e.g., Anthropic Claude Pro $\rightarrow$ Gemini Free Tier $\rightarrow$ Local Ollama).

<details>
<summary><strong>👨‍💻 View `FallbackPolicyEngine.ts` Implementation</strong></summary>

```typescript
// packages/core/src/providers/FallbackPolicyEngine.ts
import { z } from "zod";
import { Logger } from "../telemetry/Logger";

export const FallbackPolicySchema = z.object({
  policyId: z.string(),
  strategy: z.enum(["cost_optimized", "capability_first", "latency_first"]),
  chain: z.array(z.string()), // e.g., ["anthropic:claude-3-5-sonnet", "google:gemini-1.5-pro", "local:qwen"]
  onRateLimit: z.enum(["retry_then_fallback", "fallback_next"]),
  budgetMaxUsd: z.number().optional()
});

export type FallbackPolicy = z.infer<typeof FallbackPolicySchema>;

export class FallbackPolicyEngine {
  private logger = new Logger("FallbackEngine");
  
  constructor(private quotaTracker: QuotaService, private policies: FallbackPolicy[]) {}

  async executeWithFallback<T>(
    policyId: string, 
    taskExecution: (modelId: string) => Promise<T>
  ): Promise<T> {
    const policy = this.policies.find(p => p.policyId === policyId);
    if (!policy) throw new Error(`Policy ${policyId} not found`);

    for (const modelId of policy.chain) {
      if (this.quotaTracker.isExhausted(modelId)) continue;
      
      try {
        this.logger.info(`Attempting execution with ${modelId}`);
        return await taskExecution(modelId);
      } catch (error: any) {
        if (error.code === '429' || error.message.includes('rate limit')) {
          this.logger.warn(`Rate limit hit on ${modelId}. Cascading...`);
          await this.quotaTracker.markCooldown(modelId);
          continue;
        }
        throw error; // Throw non-quota related errors (e.g., syntax)
      }
    }
    throw new Error("All models in fallback chain exhausted.");
  }
}
```
</details>

### 3. The Automated Submodule Research Pipeline

To handle the massive repository of links and submodules without blocking core development, we formalize the **Research Ingestion Engine**. This runs in a background worker thread.

1.  **Queue**: You paste a URL or trigger a scan of `.gitmodules`.
2.  **Scrape**: A lightweight model (e.g., `gemini-1.5-flash` or `gpt-4o-mini`) clones/fetches the `README.md` and repo tree.
3.  **Synthesize**: The model extracts capabilities and maps them to our Reference Categories.
4.  **Index**: Results are saved to `HYPERCODE_MASTER_INDEX.jsonc` and embedded into the local ChromaDB.

<details>
<summary><strong>🤖 View `AssimilatorAgent.ts` Prompt & Logic</strong></summary>

```typescript
// packages/core/src/agents/AssimilatorAgent.ts
import { ThreadWorker } from "../runtime/worker";
import { MasterIndex } from "../types/knowledge";

const ASSIMILATOR_PROMPT = `
You are the Hypercode Research Subagent. Your goal is to analyze external AI repositories.
Given the following README and file tree, extract:
1. Core functionality (3-5 bullet points)
2. Unique capabilities not present in competitors.
3. MCP Server compatibility (Yes/No/Partial).
4. Recommendation: Should we [NATIVE_IMPLEMENT], [MCP_WRAP], [REFERENCE_ONLY], or [REJECT]?

Output strictly as a JSON object matching the HypercodeLibrarySchema.
`;

export async function processSubmoduleTask(gitUrl: string, path: string) {
  const repoData = await fetchRepoContext(path);
  const model = fallbackEngine.getCheapestTaskModel(); // e.g. Gemini Flash
  
  const result = await model.generateJSON(ASSIMILATOR_PROMPT, repoData);
  
  // Save to structured memory
  await db.library.upsert({
    url: gitUrl,
    summary: result.core_functionality,
    integration_tier: result.recommendation,
    mcp_ready: result.mcp_compatibility
  });
}
```
</details>

## Phase 122-135: Unified Execution Plan

### 🔴 Phase 122: Provider Fallback Engine (CRITICAL — Week 1)

**Every model agreed this is the single highest-impact feature.** Without it, autonomous operation is impossible.

```typescript
// packages/ai/src/fallback/engine.ts
// Consolidated design from all 7 model recommendations

interface FallbackPolicy {
  id: string;
  name: string;                    // e.g., "default-coding"
  strategy: 
    | 'ordered'                    // strict priority order
    | 'quota-aware'                // skip exhausted, prefer freshest
    | 'cost-optimized'             // cheapest available first
    | 'latency-first'             // fastest response time
    | 'capability-match'           // best fit for task type
    | 'cost_per_success_then_latency'; // GPT-5.3's hybrid suggestion
  
  chain: ProviderModelPair[];      // ordered fallback list
  
  onErrors: {
    quota_exhausted: 'fallback_next' | 'wait_and_retry';
    rate_limited: 'retry_then_fallback' | 'fallback_next';
    auth_failure: 'skip_provider' | 'refresh_and_retry';
    provider_down: 'fallback_next';
    timeout: 'retry_same' | 'fallback_next';
  };
  
  budget?: {
    maxDailyCostUsd: number;
    maxMonthlyCostUsd: number;
  };
  
  preferences?: {
    preferFreeFirst: boolean;       // Use free tiers before paid
    preferSubscriptionBeforeAPI: boolean;  // OAuth > API key
    stayInModelFamily: boolean;     // Try all providers of same model first
  };
}

interface QuotaState {
  providerId: string;
  rpm: { used: number; limit: number; resetAt: Date };
  tpm: { used: number; limit: number; resetAt: Date };
  dailyCost: { used: number; budget: number };
  isExhausted: boolean;
  lastError?: { code: string; at: Date };
  cooldownUntil?: Date;
}

// The core router — all models agreed on this pattern
class FallbackOrchestrator {
  private quotaStore: Map<string, QuotaState>;
  private policies: Map<string, FallbackPolicy>;
  
  async execute(
    task: AgenticTask, 
    policyId: string = 'default'
  ): Promise<ModelResponse> {
    const policy = this.policies.get(policyId)!;
    const chain = this.resolveChain(policy, task);
    
    for (const provider of chain) {
      const quota = this.quotaStore.get(provider.id);
      
      // Skip exhausted/cooling providers
      if (quota?.isExhausted || quota?.cooldownUntil > Date.now()) {
        this.emitTelemetry('skipped', provider, 'exhausted');
        continue;
      }
      
      try {
        const result = await this.callProvider(provider, task);
        this.trackUsage(provider, result);
        this.emitTelemetry('success', provider, result);
        return result;
      } catch (e) {
        const action = this.classifyError(e, policy);
        this.emitTelemetry('error', provider, { error: e, action });
        
        if (action === 'retry_then_fallback') {
          // Exponential backoff retry (max 2 attempts)
          const retry = await this.retryWithBackoff(provider, task, 2);
          if (retry) return retry;
        }
        
        if (action === 'fallback_next') continue;
        if (action === 'refresh_and_retry') {
          await this.refreshAuth(provider);
          continue; // Will retry this provider on next loop
        }
      }
    }
    
    throw new AllProvidersExhaustedError(chain, this.quotaStore);
  }
  
  // Kimi's suggestion: persist decision telemetry
  private emitTelemetry(
    type: string, 
    provider: ProviderModelPair, 
    data: any
  ) {
    this.eventBus.emit('provider:decision', {
      type,
      provider: provider.id,
      model: provider.model,
      timestamp: Date.now(),
      ...data
    });
  }
}
```

**Provider Registry** (all models agreed on this list):

| Provider | Auth Method | Free Tier | Subscription | API Key |
|----------|-----------|-----------|-------------|---------|
| Anthropic | OAuth (Max/Pro) + API | — | Claude Max $200/mo | ✅ |
| Google | OAuth (AI Plus) + API | Gemini Flash free | AI Plus $20/mo | ✅ |
| OpenAI | OAuth (Plus) + API | — | Plus $20/mo | ✅ |
| GitHub Copilot | OAuth/PAT | Limited free | Premium Plus | ✅ |
| xAI (Grok) | API | — | — | ✅ |
| DeepSeek | API | Free tier | — | ✅ |
| Mistral | API | Free tier | — | ✅ |
| OpenRouter | API | Free models | — | ✅ |
| OpenCode | OAuth (Black) | Sonnet free | Black tier | — |
| Cursor | OAuth | Limited free | Pro | — |
| Antigravity | OAuth (Google) | Yes | — | — |
| Local (Ollama/vLLM) | None | Unlimited | — | — |

### 🔴 Phase 123: Agentic Coding Loop (Week 1-2)

```typescript
// packages/core/src/agentic-loop/loop.ts
// The actual coding engine — what makes Hypercode a coding tool

interface AgenticLoop {
  execute(task: string, context: SessionContext): AsyncIterableIterator<LoopEvent>;
}

type LoopEvent = 
  | { type: 'thinking'; content: string }
  | { type: 'tool_call'; tool: string; params: Record<string, any> }
  | { type: 'tool_result'; tool: string; result: any; durationMs: number }
  | { type: 'edit'; file: string; diff: string }
  | { type: 'message'; content: string }
  | { type: 'context_compact'; removed: number; harvested: number }
  | { type: 'model_switch'; from: string; to: string; reason: string }
  | { type: 'complete'; summary: string }
  | { type: 'error'; error: Error; recovery?: string };

// Core tools available to the agentic loop
const CORE_TOOLS = {
  // File operations
  read_file: { /* read with line numbers, range support */ },
  write_file: { /* create or overwrite */ },
  edit_file: { /* surgical edits with search/replace blocks */ },
  list_directory: { /* recursive with gitignore respect */ },
  
  // Execution
  bash: { /* with timeout, cwd, env control */ },
  
  // Search
  grep: { /* ripgrep-powered */ },
  semantic_search: { /* embedding-based code search */ },
  find_definition: { /* LSP go-to-definition */ },
  find_references: { /* LSP find-references */ },
  
  // Git
  git_status: {},
  git_diff: {},
  git_commit: {},
  git_log: {},
  
  // Web
  web_search: {},
  fetch_url: {},
  
  // Context
  compact_context: { /* harvest + prune + summarize */ },
  store_memory: { /* save to long-term memory */ },
  recall_memory: { /* semantic memory search */ },
};

// Context manager — automatic compaction when approaching limit
class ContextManager {
  private messages: Message[] = [];
  private tokenCount: number = 0;
  private readonly tokenLimit: number;
  private readonly compactionThreshold: number; // e.g., 0.85
  
  async addMessage(msg: Message): Promise<void> {
    this.messages.push(msg);
    this.tokenCount += estimateTokens(msg);
    
    if (this.tokenCount / this.tokenLimit > this.compactionThreshold) {
      await this.autoCompact();
    }
  }
  
  private async autoCompact(): Promise<void> {
    // 1. Harvest key information into memory
    const harvested = await this.harvester.extract(this.messages);
    await this.memoryStore.storeAll(harvested);
    
    // 2. Summarize older messages
    const summary = await this.summarizer.summarize(
      this.messages.slice(0, -10) // Keep last 10 messages intact
    );
    
    // 3. Replace with summary + recent
    this.messages = [
      { role: 'system', content: summary },
      ...this.messages.slice(-10)
    ];
    
    this.tokenCount = this.messages.reduce(
      (sum, m) => sum + estimateTokens(m), 0
    );
  }
}
```

```tsx
// apps/web/src/app/overview/page.tsx

export default function OverviewPage() {

      </div>

          <RecentActivityFeed />

    </div>

// SystemHealthStrip — real-time hardware monitoring
function SystemHealthStrip() {
  const { data } = api.system.health.useQuery(undefined, { 
    refetchInterval: 2000 
  });
  
  return (
    <div className="flex gap-4 p-3 bg-slate-900/50 rounded-lg border border-slate-700">
      <MetricPill label="CPU" value={data?.cpu} unit="%" 
        color={data?.cpu > 80 ? 'red' : data?.cpu > 50 ? 'yellow' : 'green'} />
      <MetricPill label="RAM" value={data?.ram} unit="%" 
        color={data?.ram > 85 ? 'red' : 'green'} />
      <MetricPill label="GPU" value={data?.gpu} unit="%" />
      <MetricPill label="Disk" value={data?.disk} unit="%" />
      <MetricPill label="MCP" value={data?.mcpServers} unit=" active" />
      <MetricPill label="Sessions" value={data?.activeSessions} unit=" running" />
      <MetricPill label="Memory" value={data?.memoryCount} unit=" entries" />
    </div>
  );
}

// ProviderQuotaCard — the fallback chain visualizer
function ProviderQuotaCard() {
  const { data: providers } = api.providers.quotaStatus.useQuery();
  const { data: chain } = api.providers.fallbackChain.useQuery();
  
  return (
    <Card className="bg-slate-900 border-slate-700">
      <CardHeader>
        <CardTitle className="flex items-center gap-2">
          <Zap className="h-5 w-5 text-yellow-400" />
          Provider Quotas
        </CardTitle>
        {chain && (
          <p className="text-xs text-slate-400">
            Fallback: {chain.map(c => c.name).join(' → ')}
            <Button variant="ghost" size="xs" className="ml-2">Edit</Button>
          </p>
        )}
      </CardHeader>
      <CardContent className="space-y-3">
        {providers?.map(p => (
          <ProviderQuotaBar key={p.id} provider={p} />
        ))}
      </CardContent>
    </Card>
  );
}

function ProviderQuotaBar({ provider }: { provider: ProviderQuota }) {
  const pctUsed = (provider.rpm.used / provider.rpm.limit) * 100;
  const color = pctUsed > 90 ? 'bg-red-500' : pctUsed > 70 ? 'bg-yellow-500' : 'bg-green-500';
  
  return (
    <div className="space-y-1">
      <div className="flex justify-between text-sm">
        <span className="flex items-center gap-2">
          <ProviderIcon id={provider.id} />
          {provider.name}
          {provider.authMethod === 'oauth' && (
            <Badge variant="outline" className="text-[10px]">
              {provider.oauthConnected ? '✅ Connected' : '⚠️ Not connected'}
            </Badge>
          )}
        </span>
        <span className="text-slate-400">
          {provider.rpm.used}/{provider.rpm.limit} RPM
          {provider.resetIn && ` · Resets ${provider.resetIn}`}
        </span>
      </div>
      <div className="h-2 bg-slate-700 rounded-full overflow-hidden">
        <div className={`h-full ${color} rounded-full transition-all`} 
             style={{ width: `${pctUsed}%` }} />
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
```

### 🔴 Phase 125: Session Supervisor & Auto-Restart (Week 2)

```typescript
// packages/core/src/sessions/supervisor.ts
// Consolidated from Qwen's SessionGuardian + GPT-5.4's ExecutionSupervisor

import { ChildProcess, spawn } from 'child_process';
import { EventEmitter } from 'events';

interface SessionRuntime {
  id: string;
  name: string;
  harness: 'hypercode-native' | 'opencode' | 'claude-code' | 'codex' | 
           'gemini-cli' | 'superai-cli' | 'codebuff' | string;
  status: 'starting' | 'running' | 'paused' | 'crashed' | 'stopped';
  
  // Bindings
  cwd: string;
  worktree?: string;
  providerId?: string;
  modelPolicyId?: string;
  
  // Supervision
  autoRestart: boolean;
  maxRestarts: number;
  restartCount: number;
  restartBackoffMs: number;
  crashLoopDetected: boolean;
  
  // Telemetry
  pid?: number;
  startedAt?: Date;
  lastActivityAt?: Date;
  tokensUsed?: number;
  costUsd?: number;
  
  // Process handle (not serialized)
  process?: ChildProcess;
}

class SessionSupervisor extends EventEmitter {
  private sessions = new Map<string, SessionRuntime>();
  private heartbeatInterval: NodeJS.Timer;
  
  constructor(private db: Database, private eventBus: EventBus) {
    super();
    // Restore sessions from DB on startup
    this.restoreSessions();
    // Heartbeat check every 10s
    this.heartbeatInterval = setInterval(() => this.checkHealth(), 10000);
  }
  
  async startSession(config: StartSessionConfig): Promise<SessionRuntime> {
    const session: SessionRuntime = {
      id: crypto.randomUUID(),
      name: config.name,
      harness: config.harness,
      status: 'starting',
      cwd: config.cwd,
      autoRestart: config.autoRestart ?? true,
      maxRestarts: config.maxRestarts ?? 10,
      restartCount: 0,
      restartBackoffMs: 1000,
      crashLoopDetected: false,
    };
    
    this.sessions.set(session.id, session);
    await this.spawnProcess(session);
    await this.db.sessions.upsert(session);
    
    return session;
  }
  
  private async spawnProcess(session: SessionRuntime): Promise<void> {
    const cmd = this.getCommand(session.harness, session);
    const proc = spawn(cmd.bin, cmd.args, {
      cwd: session.cwd,
      env: { ...process.env, ...cmd.env },
      stdio: ['pipe', 'pipe', 'pipe'],
    });
    
    session.process = proc;
    session.pid = proc.pid;
    session.status = 'running';
    session.startedAt = new Date();
    
    proc.stdout?.on('data', (data: Buffer) => {
      session.lastActivityAt = new Date();
      this.eventBus.emit('session:output', { 
        sessionId: session.id, 
        data: data.toString(), 
        stream: 'stdout' 
      });
    });
    
    proc.stderr?.on('data', (data: Buffer) => {
      this.eventBus.emit('session:output', { 
        sessionId: session.id, 
        data: data.toString(), 
        stream: 'stderr' 
      });
    });
    
    proc.on('exit', (code, signal) => {
      session.status = 'crashed';
      session.process = undefined;
      
      this.eventBus.emit('session:exit', { 
        sessionId: session.id, code, signal 
      });
      
      if (session.autoRestart && !session.crashLoopDetected) {
        this.scheduleRestart(session);
      }
    });
    
    this.eventBus.emit('session:started', { 
      sessionId: session.id, 
      pid: proc.pid 
    });
  }
  
  private scheduleRestart(session: SessionRuntime): void {
    session.restartCount++;
    
    if (session.restartCount >= session.maxRestarts) {
      session.crashLoopDetected = true;
      session.status = 'stopped';
      this.eventBus.emit('session:crash_loop', { sessionId: session.id });
      return;
    }
    
    const delay = Math.min(
      session.restartBackoffMs * Math.pow(2, session.restartCount - 1),
      30000 // Max 30s backoff
    );
    
    this.eventBus.emit('session:restarting', { 
      sessionId: session.id, 
      delayMs: delay,
      attempt: session.restartCount 
    });
    
    setTimeout(() => this.spawnProcess(session), delay);
  }
  
  private getCommand(
    harness: string, 
    session: SessionRuntime
  ): { bin: string; args: string[]; env: Record<string, string> } {
    switch (harness) {
      case 'hypercode-native':
        return { bin: 'node', args: ['packages/cli/dist/index.js', '--dir', session.cwd], env: {} };
      case 'opencode':
        return { bin: 'opencode', args: ['--dir', session.cwd], env: {} };
      case 'claude-code':
        return { bin: 'claude', args: ['--dir', session.cwd], env: {} };
      case 'codex':
        return { bin: 'codex', args: [session.cwd], env: {} };
      case 'gemini-cli':
        return { bin: 'gemini', args: ['--dir', session.cwd], env: {} };
      default:
        return { bin: harness, args: ['--dir', session.cwd], env: {} };
    }
  }
  
  // WebSocket streaming to dashboard
  getSessionStream(sessionId: string): ReadableStream<SessionEvent> {
    // Returns a stream that the dashboard can consume via WebSocket
    // for real-time log viewing
  }
  
  async broadcastToAll(message: string): Promise<void> {
    for (const [id, session] of this.sessions) {
      if (session.status === 'running' && session.process?.stdin) {
        session.process.stdin.write(message + '\n');
      }
    }
  }
}
```

**Sessions Dashboard Panel:**

```tsx
// apps/web/src/app/sessions/page.tsx

export default function SessionsPage() {
  const { data: sessions } = api.sessions.list.useQuery();
  const startSession = api.sessions.start.useMutation();
  const restartSession = api.sessions.restart.useMutation();
  
  return (
    <div className="flex flex-col gap-6 p-6">
      {/* Header with actions */}

function SessionCard({ session }: { session: SessionRuntime }) {
  const [showTerminal, setShowTerminal] = useState(false);
  
  return (
    <Card className="bg-slate-900 border-slate-700">
      <CardHeader className="pb-2">
        <div className="flex justify-between items-start">
          <div>
            <div className="flex items-center gap-2">
              <StatusDot status={session.status} />
              <span className="font-mono text-sm">{session.cwd}</span>
            </div>
            <p className="text-xs text-slate-400 mt-1">
              {session.harness} · {session.providerId || 'auto'} · 
              {session.tokensUsed?.toLocaleString() || 0} tokens ·
              ${session.costUsd?.toFixed(2) || '0.00'}
            </p>
          </div>
          <div className="flex gap-1">
            <Button size="icon" variant="ghost" 
              onClick={() => setShowTerminal(!showTerminal)}>
              <Terminal className="h-4 w-4" />
            </Button>
            <Button size="icon" variant="ghost"
              onClick={() => restartSession.mutate(session.id)}>
              <RotateCw className="h-4 w-4" />
            </Button>
            <Button size="icon" variant="ghost"
              onClick={() => stopSession.mutate(session.id)}>
              <Square className="h-4 w-4" />
            </Button>
          </div>
        </div>
      </CardHeader>
      {showTerminal && (
        <CardContent className="pt-0">
          <div className="h-48 bg-black rounded-lg overflow-hidden">
            <WebTerminal sessionId={session.id} />
          </div>
        </CardContent>
      )}
    </Card>
  );
}
```

### 🟡 Phase 127-131: MCP Router Polish (Week 3-4)

```typescript
// packages/mcp/src/toon-formatter.ts
// TOON Format — Tool-Optimized Output Notation

export function formatToolAsTOON(tool: MCPTool): string {
  // Convert verbose JSON schema to minimal context representation
  // Example: "read_file(path:str, range?:str) → str — Read file content"
  const params = tool.inputSchema.properties 
    ? Object.entries(tool.inputSchema.properties)
        .map(([name, schema]: [string, any]) => {
          const required = tool.inputSchema.required?.includes(name);
          const type = schema.type || 'any';
          return `${name}${required ? '' : '?'}:${type}`;
        })
        .join(', ')
    : '';
  
  return `${tool.name}(${params}) → ${tool.outputType || 'any'} — ${tool.description}`;
}

// Code Mode — represent tools as callable functions
export function formatToolAsCode(tool: MCPTool): string {
  return `async function ${tool.name}(${formatParams(tool)}): Promise<${tool.outputType || 'any'}> { /* ${tool.description} */ }`;
}

// Progressive Tool Disclosure
export class ProgressiveToolLoader {
  private allTools: MCPTool[];
  private disclosedTools: Set<string> = new Set();
  private embeddings: Map<string, number[]> = new Map();
  
  getRelevantTools(taskDescription: string, maxTools: number = 20): MCPTool[] {
    // 1. Always include essential tools (file, bash, search)
    const essential = this.allTools.filter(t => t.essential);
    
    // 2. Semantic search for task-relevant tools
    const taskEmbedding = this.embed(taskDescription);
    const ranked = this.allTools
      .filter(t => !t.essential)
      .map(t => ({
        tool: t,
        score: cosineSimilarity(taskEmbedding, this.embeddings.get(t.name)!)
      }))
      .sort((a, b) => b.score - a.score)
      .slice(0, maxTools - essential.length);
    
    return [...essential, ...ranked.map(r => r.tool)];
  }
}
```

## Process Architecture (All Models Agreed)

```
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     HYPERCODE MAIN PROCESS                         │
│  Express + tRPC + WebSocket + Event Bus                       │
│  Orchestrates everything, never does heavy compute            │
├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                               │
│  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌────────────────────┐ │
│  │ Worker Pool  │  │ MCP Server   │  │ Session Runtimes   │ │
│  │ (Threads)    │  │ Pool (Child  │  │ (Child Processes)  │ │
│  │              │  │  Processes)  │  │                    │ │
│  │ • Planning   │  │ • filesystem │  │ • hypercode-native #1   │ │
│  │ • Ranking    │  │ • memory     │  │ • opencode #2      │ │
│  │ • Embedding  │  │ • browser    │  │ • codex #3         │ │
│  │ • Compaction │  │ • git        │  │ • gemini-cli #4    │ │
│  │ • Summarize  │  │ • search     │  │ • claude-code #5   │ │
│  │              │  │ • +42 more   │  │                    │ │
│  │ Crash →      │  │ Crash →      │  │ Crash →            │ │
│  │ kill thread  │  │ restart proc │  │ restart w/ backoff  │ │
│  └──────────────┘  └──────────────┘  └────────────────────┘ │
│                                                               │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                  WebSocket Hub                            │ │
│  │  • Dashboard real-time updates (all panels)               │ │
│  │  • Session output streaming (xterm.js in browser)         │ │
│  │  • Agent ↔ Agent communication                            │ │
│  │  • Provider quota change notifications                    │ │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                               │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │               Redis (optional, for scale)                 │ │
│  │  • Swarm coordination pub/sub                             │ │
│  │  • Cross-process state sync                               │ │
│  │  • Task queue for research pipeline                       │ │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Isolation Rules** (unanimous):
- Agent/model crash → kills only that worker thread, auto-restart
- MCP server crash → child process restarts, circuit breaker after 3 failures
- CLI session crash → auto-restart with exponential backoff, max 10 retries
- Main process → never crashes from child/worker failures (supervisor pattern)

**Assistant - --**

Based on the comprehensive analysis across all model providers, here is the **definitive Phase 122 implementation blueprint** to achieve UI/functionality parity and the critical Provider Fallback system.

---

## 1. Architecture Decision: The Cellular TypeScript OS

**Decision: Pure TypeScript/Node.js with Strategic Process Isolation**

We remain TypeScript-native for ecosystem compatibility (MCP SDK, Vercel AI SDK, shared types with React dashboard), but implement a **"Cellular Architecture"** for fault tolerance:

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    CONTROL PLANE (Main Process)                 │
│  packages/core                                                  │
│  • Express/tRPC/WebSocket API                                   │
│  • ProviderRouter & FallbackPolicyEngine                        │
│  • SessionRuntimeRegistry                                       │
│  • Configuration/Auth                                           │
└──────────────┬──────────────────────────────┬───────────────────┘
               │                              │
    ┌──────────▼──────────┐      ┌───────────▼────────────┐
    │   AGENT WORKERS     │      │   SESSION RUNTIMES     │
    │   (Worker Threads)  │      │   (Child Processes)    │
    │  • Prompt planning  │      │  • External CLIs       │
    │  • Context ranking  │      │  • MCP Servers         │
    │  • Tool selection   │      │  • Browser automation  │
    │  • Crash isolation  │      │  • Code sandboxes      │
    └──────────┬──────────┘      └───────────┬────────────┘
               │                              │
    ┌──────────▼──────────────────────────────▼────────────┐
    │              REDIS MESH BUS (Pub/Sub)                │
    │   • Cross-cell state sync                            │
    │   • Swarm coordination                               │
    │   • Artifact federation                              │
    └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Crash Boundaries:**
- **Level 1**: Try/catch around tool calls (expected)
- **Level 2**: Worker termination + respawn (model crash)
- **Level 3**: Process restart + session recovery (CLI/MCP crash)
- **Level 4**: Circuit breakers (provider quota exhaustion)

---

## 2. Phase 122: Critical Implementation Path

### P0: Provider Fallback Engine (Unblocks Everything)

**New Service**: `packages/core/src/providers/FallbackPolicyEngine.ts`

```typescript
interface FallbackChain {
  chainId: string;
  strategy: 'cost-optimized' | 'latency-first' | 'quota-aware' | 'quality-preserve';
  providers: ProviderConfig[];
  quotaTracking: Map<string, QuotaStatus>;
  onExhaustion: 'pause' | 'local-fallback' | 'notify-user';
}

export class FallbackPolicyEngine extends EventEmitter {
  // Real-time quota monitoring
  async executeWithFallback(task: Task, chain: FallbackChain): AsyncIterable<StreamChunk> {
    for (const provider of chain.providers) {
      try {
        return await this.execute(task, provider);
      } catch (e) {
        if (e.code === 'QUOTA_EXHAUSTED' || e.code === 'RATE_LIMIT') {
          this.emit('provider_exhausted', { provider, task });
          await this.quotaTracker.markExhausted(provider.id);
          continue; // Seamless fallback
        }
        throw e;
      }
    }
    throw new Error('All providers exhausted');
  }
}
```

**SQLite Schema** (`database/quota_tracking.sql`):
```sql
CREATE TABLE provider_quotas (
  provider_id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
  rpm_used INTEGER,
  rpm_limit INTEGER,
  tpm_used INTEGER,
  tpm_limit INTEGER,
  daily_cost_usd REAL,
  daily_budget_usd REAL,
  reset_at TIMESTAMP,
  is_exhausted BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
  last_error TEXT
);
```

### P0: Session Guardian Service

**New Service**: `packages/core/src/sessions/SessionGuardian.ts`

Manages external CLI harnesses (opencode, superai-cli, codebuff, etc.) with auto-restart:

```typescript
interface SessionRuntime {
  sessionId: string;
  harnessType: 'hypercode-native' | 'opencode' | 'superai-cli' | 'codex' | 'claude-code';
  process?: ChildProcess;
  worktreePath: string;
  providerChain: FallbackChain;
  autoRestart: boolean;
  supervisorMode: 'single' | 'council' | 'fallback-cycle';
  state: 'running' | 'crashed' | 'paused' | 'recovering';
}

export class SessionGuardian extends EventEmitter {
  private sessions: Map<string, SessionRuntime> = new Map();
  
  async spawnSession(config: SessionConfig): Promise<string> {
    // Spawn in isolated child process with PTY support
    const proc = spawn(config.command, config.args, {
      cwd: config.worktree,
      env: { ...process.env, ...config.env },
      detached: false
    });
    
    // Monitor with heartbeat
    const sessionId = crypto.randomUUID();
    this.sessions.set(sessionId, { ...config, process: proc, state: 'running' });
    
    proc.on('exit', (code) => this.handleCrash(sessionId, code));
    return sessionId;
  }
  
  private async handleCrash(sessionId: string, code: number) {
    const session = this.sessions.get(sessionId);
    if (session?.autoRestart) {
      this.emit('session_crash', { sessionId, code });
      await this.respawnWithBackoff(sessionId);
    }
  }
}
```

### P1: Dashboard Reality Closure

**New Routes** (`apps/web/src/app/dashboard/`):

1. **Mission Control** (`/dashboard/mission-control`)
   - System health (CPU/RAM/GPU)
   - Active sessions grid with live status
   - Provider quota bars with visual warnings
   - Recent crash/restart events

2. **Provider Matrix** (`/dashboard/providers`)
   - OAuth connection buttons (Claude Max, Google AI Plus, Copilot Premium, OpenCode Black)
   - Live quota burn visualization
   - Fallback chain editor (drag-drop reordering)
   - "Test Connection" functionality

3. **Session Orchestrator** (`/dashboard/sessions`)
   - Grid view of all CLI sessions (local + cloud)
   - Terminal emulation via `xterm.js` for each session
   - Auto-restart toggle per session
   - "Broadcast to All" command input
   - Worktree binding status

4. **MCP Control Plane** (`/dashboard/mcp`)
   - Server list with health indicators (latency, uptime)
   - Live traffic inspector (WebSocket stream of JSON-RPC)
   - Tool browser with semantic search
   - Namespace management UI

### Provider Quota Card Component

```typescript
// apps/web/src/components/dashboard/ProviderQuotaCard.tsx
export function ProviderQuotaCard({ providerId }: { providerId: string }) {
  const { data: quota } = api.providers.getQuota.useQuery(providerId);
  const { mutate: connectOAuth } = api.providers.connectOAuth.useMutation();
  
  return (
    <Card className={quota?.isExhausted ? "border-red-500" : "border-green-500"}>
      <CardHeader>
        <div className="flex justify-between">
          <CardTitle>{providerId}</CardTitle>
          {quota?.isOAuth ? (
            <Badge variant="outline">Connected</Badge>
          ) : (
            <Button onClick={() => connectOAuth(providerId)}>Connect</Button>
          )}
        </div>
      </CardHeader>
      <CardContent>
        <div className="space-y-2">
          <QuotaBar label="RPM" used={quota.rpmUsed} limit={quota.rpmLimit} />
          <QuotaBar label="Daily Cost" used={quota.dailyCost} limit={quota.dailyBudget} currency="$" />
          {quota.isExhausted && (
            <Alert variant="destructive">
              <AlertCircle className="h-4 w-4" />
              <AlertDescription>Quota exhausted. Fallback active.</AlertDescription>
            </Alert>
          )}
        </div>
      </CardContent>
    </Card>
  );
}
```

### Session Supervisor Grid

```typescript
// apps/web/src/components/dashboard/SessionGrid.tsx
export function SessionGrid() {
  const { data: sessions } = api.sessions.list.useQuery();
  const { mutate: restartSession } = api.sessions.restart.useMutation();
  
  return (
    <div className="grid grid-cols-1 md:grid-cols-2 lg:grid-cols-3 gap-4">
      {sessions?.map(session => (
        <SessionCard 
          key={session.id}
          session={session}
          onRestart={() => restartSession(session.id)}
          terminalRef={el => attachXTerm(session.id, el)}
        />
      ))}
    </div>
  );
}
```

## 4. Submodule Research & Indexing Pipeline

To handle the 932+ submodules systematically without blocking development:

**Tiered Integration Strategy**:

| Tier | Count | Action | Example |
|------|-------|--------|---------|
| **T1: Native Core** | ~30 | Full integration into `packages/core` | MetaMCP (fork features), Jules-autopilot (fork features) |
| **T2: Plugin Adapters** | ~50 | Wrapped as plugins in `packages/plugins` | OpenCode, Claude Code, mem0, ChromaDB |
| **T3: MCP Directory** | ~200 | Indexed in `mcp.json` catalog | Various MCP servers |
| **T4: Reference Only** | ~400 | Documented in `references/` | Code examples, research papers |
| **T5: Rejected** | ~250 | Logged in `references/rejected_links.txt` | Noise, duplicates |

**Automated Research Subagent** (deploy via `packages/research`):

```typescript
// packages/research/src/LinkIngestionService.ts
interface ResearchTask {
  url: string;
  priority: number;
  category?: string;
}

export class LinkIngestionService {
  async processLink(task: ResearchTask) {
    // 1. Scrape (lightweight subagent: Gemini Flash)
    const summary = await this.scrapeAndSummarize(task.url);
    
    // 2. Classify
    const category = await this.classifyTool(summary);
    
    // 3. Decision
    if (category.relevance > 8) {
      await this.addAsSubmodule(task.url, summary);
      await this.scaffoldIntegration(summary);
    } else if (category.relevance > 5) {
      await this.indexForReference(summary);
    } else {
      await this.rejectLink(task.url, 'low_relevance');
    }
    
    // 4. Update HYPERCODE_MASTER_INDEX.jsonc
    await this.updateMasterIndex(summary);
  }
}
```
